## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

## Your Task

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the crossrepo domain.

I am thinking...: Now I have a clear picture of the chain. Let me also check the recreate.go file and the util directory for completeness. Let me also look at the deployment util directory.

The chain is:
1. **Deployment Controller** (`pkg/controller/deployment/deployment_controller.go`):
   - `syncDeployment` is the main reconcile function
   - It calls `rolloutRolling` or `rolloutRecreate` based on strategy
   
2. **Deployment sync** (`pkg/controller/deployment/sync.go`):
   - `getNewReplicaSet` creates a new ReplicaSet via `dc.client.AppsV1().ReplicaSets(d.Namespace).Create()`
   - `getAllReplicaSetsAndSyncRevision` calls `getNewReplicaSet`
   
3. **Deployment rolling** (`pkg/controller/deployment/rolling.go`):
   - `rolloutRolling` calls `getAllReplicaSetsAndSyncRevision` (with createIfNotExisted=true) which creates the RS
   - Then calls `reconcileNewReplicaSet` to scale it up

4. **ReplicaSet Controller** (`pkg/controller/replicaset/replica_set.go`):
   - `syncReplicaSet` is the main reconcile function
   - It calls `manageReplicas` which calls `rsc.podControl.CreatePods()`

5. **Controller Utils** (`pkg/controller/controller_utils.go`):
   - `RealPodControl.CreatePods` → `CreatePodsWithGenerateName` → `createPods`
   - `createPods` calls `r.KubeClient.CoreV1().Pods(namespace).Create()`

6. **API Server Pod Storage** (`pkg/registry/core/pod/storage/storage.go`):
   - The `REST` struct embeds `*genericregistry.Store`
   - The `Create` method is inherited from `genericregistry.Store`

7. **Generic Registry Store** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/registry/generic/registry/store.go`):
   - `Store.Create` → `store.create` → `e.Storage.Create` (writes to etcd)

342026-03-08T20:32:03.252656agentmessage-
The answer file has been created at `/workspace/answer.json`. Here's a summary of the complete chain I traced:

## Deployment Spec Change → ReplicaSet Creation → Pod Creation Chain

### 1. Deployment Controller Reconcile
**`pkg/controller/deployment/deployment_controller.go`** — `syncDeployment`
- Triggered when a Deployment is updated (via informer → `updateDeployment` → enqueue)
- Dispatches to `rolloutRolling` or `rolloutRecreate` based on strategy

### 2. ReplicaSet Creation
**`pkg/controller/deployment/rolling.go`** — `rolloutRolling`  
**`pkg/controller/deployment/sync.go`** — `getAllReplicaSetsAndSyncRevision` → `getNewReplicaSet`
- `getNewReplicaSet` constructs a new `apps.ReplicaSet` with the pod template hash as name suffix
- Calls `dc.client.AppsV1().ReplicaSets(...).Create()` to persist it via the API server
- Then `reconcileNewReplicaSet` scales the RS up via `scaleReplicaSetAndRecordEvent`

### 3. ReplicaSet Controller Reconcile
**`pkg/controller/replicaset/replica_set.go`** — `syncReplicaSet` → `manageReplicas`
- Triggered when the new RS is created/updated
- `manageReplicas` computes pod deficit and calls `rsc.podControl.CreatePods()` in a `slowStartBatch`

### 4. Pod Creation in the API Server
**`pkg/controller/controller_utils.go`** — `RealPodControl.CreatePods` → `createPods`
- Calls `r.KubeClient.CoreV1().Pods(namespace).Create()` → HTTP POST to API server

**`pkg/registry/core/pod/storage/storage.go`** — `REST` (embeds `genericregistry.Store`)  
**`pkg/registry/core/pod/strategy.go`** — `PrepareForCreate` (pod creation strategy)  
**`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/registry/generic/registry/store.go`** — `Store.Create` → `e.Storage.Create()` (writes to etcd)

bumping collisionCount to resolve it\\\\\\\", \\\\\\\"deployment\\\\\\\", klog.KObj(d), \\\\\\\"oldCollisionCount\\\\\\\", preCollisionCount, \\\\\\\"newCollisionCount\\\\\\\", *d.Status.CollisionCount)\\\\n259: \\\\t\\\\t}\\\\n260: \\\\t\\\\treturn nil, err\\\\n261: \\\\tcase errors.HasStatusCause(err, v1.NamespaceTerminatingCause):\\\\n262: \\\\t\\\\t// if the namespace is terminating, all subsequent creates will fail and we can safely do nothing\\\\n263: \\\\t\\\\treturn nil, err\\\\n264: \\\\tcase err != nil:\\\\n265: \\\\t\\\\tmsg := fmt.Sprintf(\\\\\\\"Failed to create new replica set %q: %v\\\\\\\", newRS.Name, err)\\\\n266: \\\\t\\\\tif deploymentutil.HasProgressDeadline(d) {\\\\n267: \\\\t\\\\t\\\\tcond := deploymentutil.NewDeploymentCondition(apps.DeploymentProgressing, v1.ConditionFalse, deploymentutil.FailedRSCreateReason, msg)\\\\n268: \\\\t\\\\t\\\\tdeploymentutil.SetDeploymentCondition(\\\\u0026d.Status, *cond)\\\\n269: \\\\t\\\\t\\\\t// We don't really care about this error at this point, since we have a bigger issue to report.\\\\n270: \\\\t\\\\t\\\\t// TODO: Identify which errors are permanent and switch DeploymentIsFailed to take into account\\\\n271: \\\\t\\\\t\\\\t// these reasons as well. Related issue: https://github.com/kubernetes/kubernetes/issues/18568\\\\n272: \\\\t\\\\t\\\\t_, _ = dc.client.AppsV1().Deployments(d.Namespace).UpdateStatus(ctx, d, metav1.UpdateOptions{})\\\\n273: \\\\t\\\\t}\\\\n274: \\\\t\\\\tdc.eventRecorder.Eventf(d, v1.EventTypeWarning, deploymentutil.FailedRSCreateReason, msg)\\\\n275: \\\\t\\\\treturn nil, err\\\\n276: \\\\t}\\\\n277: \\\\tif !alreadyExists \\\\u0026\\\\u0026 newReplicasCount \\\\u003e 0 {\\\\n278: \\\\t\\\\tdc.eventRecorder.Eventf(d, v1.EventTypeNormal, \\\\\\\"ScalingReplicaSet\\\\\\\", \\\\\\\"Scaled up replica set %s from 0 to %d\\\\\\\", createdRS.Name, newReplicasCount)\\\\n279: \\\\t}\\\\n280: \\\\n281: \\\\tneedsUpdate := deploymentutil.SetDeploymentRevision(d, newRevision)\\\\n282: \\\\tif !alreadyExists \\\\u0026\\\\u0026 deploymentutil.HasProgressDeadline(d) {\\\\n283: \\\\t\\\\tmsg := fmt.Sprintf(\\\\\\\"Created new replica set %q\\\\\\\", createdRS.Name)\\\\n284: \\\\t\\\\tcondition := deploymentutil.NewDeploymentCondition(apps.DeploymentProgressing, v1.ConditionTrue, deploymentutil.NewReplicaSetReason, msg)\\\\n285: \\\\t\\\\tdeploymentutil.SetDeploymentCondition(\\\\u0026d.Status, *condition)\\\\n286: \\\\t\\\\tneedsUpdate = true\\\\n287: \\\\t}\\\\n288: \\\\tif needsUpdate {\\\\n289: \\\\t\\\\t_, err = dc.client.AppsV1().Deployments(d.Namespace).UpdateStatus(ctx, d, metav1.UpdateOptions{})\\\\n290: \\\\t}\\\\n291: \\\\treturn createdRS, err\\\\n292: }\\\\n293: \\\\n294: // scale scales proportionally in order to mitigate risk. Otherwise, scaling up can increase the size\\\\n295: // of the new replica set and scaling down can decrease the sizes of the old ones, both of which would\\\\n296: // have the effect of hastening the rollout progress, which could produce a higher proportion of unavailable\\\\n297: // replicas in the event of a problem with the rolled out template. Should run only on scaling events or\\\\n298: // when a deployment is paused and not during the normal rollout process.\\\\n299: func (dc *DeploymentController) scale(ctx context.Context, deployment *apps.Deployment, newRS *apps.ReplicaSet, oldRSs []*apps.ReplicaSet) error {\\\\n300: \\\\t// If there is only one active replica set then we should scale that up to the full count of the\\\\n301: \\\\t// deployment. These replicas should be distributed proportionally to the active\\\\n335: \\\\t\\\\t// replica sets.\\\\n336: \\\\t\\\\tdeploymentReplicasToAdd := allowedSize - allRSsReplicas\\\\n337: \\\\n338: \\\\t\\\\t// The additional replicas should be distributed proportionally amongst the active\\\\n339: \\\\t\\\\t// replica sets from the larger to the smaller in size replica set. Scaling direction\\\\n340: \\\\t\\\\t// drives what happens in case we are trying to scale replica sets of the same size.\\\\n341: \\\\t\\\\t// In such a case when scaling up, we should scale up newer replica sets first, and\\\\n342: \\\\t\\\\t// when scaling down, we should scale down older replica sets first.\\\\n343: \\\\t\\\\tswitch {\\\\n344: \\\\t\\\\tcase deploymentReplicasToAdd \\\\u003e 0:\\\\n345: \\\\t\\\\t\\\\tsort.Sort(controller.ReplicaSetsBySizeNewer(allRSs))\\\\n346: \\\\n347: \\\\t\\\\tcase deploymentReplicasToAdd \\\\u003c 0:\\\\n348: {\\\\n358: \\\\t\\\\t\\\\trs := allRSs[i]\\\\n359: \\\\n360: \\\\t\\\\t\\\\t// Estimate proportions if we have replicas to add, otherwise simply populate\\\\n361: \\\\t\\\\t\\\\t// nameToSize with the current sizes for each replica set.\\\\n362: \\\\t\\\\t\\\\tif deploymentReplicasToAdd != 0 {\\\\n363: \\\\t\\\\t\\\\t\\\\tproportion := deploymentutil.GetReplicaSetProportion(logger, rs, *deployment, deploymentReplicasToAdd, deploymentReplicasAdded)\\\\n364: \\\\n365: \\\\t\\\\t\\\\t\\\\tnameToSize[rs.Name] = *(rs.Spec.Replicas) + proportion\\\\n366: \\\\t\\\\t\\\\t\\\\tdeploymentReplicasAdded += proportion\\\\n367: \\\\t\\\\t\\\\t} else {\\\\n368: \\\\t\\\\t\\\\t\\\\tnameToSize[rs.Name] = *(rs.Spec.Replicas)\\\\n369: \\\\t\\\\t\\\\t}\\\\n370: \\\\t\\\\t}\\\\n371: \\\\n372: \\\\t\\\\t// Update all replica sets\\\\n373: \\\\t\\\\tfor i := range allRSs {\\\\n374: \\\\t\\\\t\\\\trs := allRSs[i]\\\\n375: \\\\n376: \\\\t\\\\t\\\\t// Add/remove any leftovers to the largest replica set.\\\\n377: However, 13 - 8 - 5 = 0, so the oldRS won't be scaled down.\\n118: \\t// * The user notices the crashloop and does kubectl rollout undo to rollback.\\n119: \\t// * newRSPodsUnavailable is 1, since we rolled back to the good replica set, so maxScaledDown = 13 - 8 - 1 = 4. 4 of the crashlooping pods will be scaled down.\\n120: \\t// * The total number of pods will then be 9 and the newRS can be scaled up to 10.\\n121: \\t//\\n122: \\t// case 2:\\n123: \\t// Same example, but pushing a new pod template instead of rolling back (aka \\\"roll over\\\"):\\n124: \\t// * The new replica set created must start with 0 replicas because allPodsCount is already at 13.\\n125: \\t// * However, newRSPodsUnavailable would also be 0, so the 2 old replica sets could be scaled down by 5 (13 - 8 - 0), which would then\\n126: \\t// allow the new replica set to be scaled up by 5.\\n127: \\tminAvailable := *(deployment.Spec.Replicas) - maxUnavailable\\n128: \\tnewRSUnavailablePodCount := *(newRS.Spec.Replicas) - newRS.Status.AvailableReplicas\\n129: \\tmaxScaledDown := allPodsCount - minAvailable - newRSUnavailablePodCount\\n130: \\tif maxScaledDown <= 0 {\\n131: \\t\\treturn false, nil\\n132: \\t}\\n133: \\n134: \\t// Clean up unhealthy replicas first, otherwise unhealthy replicas will block deployment\\n135: \\t// and cause timeout. This ensures that unhealthy replicas will\\n160: \\t// been deleted first and won't increase unavailability.\\n161: \\ttotalScaledDown := int32(0)\\n162: \\tfor i, targetRS := range oldRSs {\\n163: \\t\\tif totalScaledDown >= maxCleanupCount {\\n164: \\t\\t\\tbreak\\n165: \\t\\t}\\n166: \\t\\tif *(targetRS.Spec.Replicas) == 0 {\\n167: \\t\\t\\t// cannot scale down this replica set.\\n168: \\t\\t\\tcontinue\\n169: \\t\\t}\\n170: \\t\\tlogger.V(4).Info(\\\"Found available pods in old RS\\\", \\\"replicaSet\\\", klog.KObj(targetRS), \\\"availableReplicas\\\", targetRS.Status.AvailableReplicas)\\n171: \\t\\tif *(targetRS.Spec.Replicas) == targetRS.Status.AvailableReplicas {\\n172: \\t\\t\\t// no unhealthy replicas found, no scaling required.\\n173: \\t\\t\\tcontinue\\n174: \\t\\t}\\n175: \\n176: \\t\\tscaledDownCount := min(maxCleanupCount-totalScaledDown, *(targetRS.Spec.Replicas)-targetRS.Status.AvailableReplicas)\\n177: \\t\\tnewReplicasCount := *(targetRS.Spec.Replicas) - scaledDownCount\\n178: \\t\\tif newReplicasCount > *(targetRS.Spec.Replicas) {\\n179: \\t\\t\\treturn nil, 0, fmt.Errorf(\\\"when cleaning up unhealthy replicas, got invalid request to scale down %s/%s %d -> %d\\\", targetRS.Namespace, targetRS.Name, *(targetRS.Spec.Replicas), newReplicasCount)\\n180: \\t\\t}\\n181: \\t\\t_, updatedOldRS, err := dc.scaleReplicaSetAndRecordEvent(ctx, targetRS, newReplicasCount, deployment)\\n182: \\t\\tif err != nil {\\n183: \\t\\t\\treturn nil, totalScaledDown, err\\n184: \\t\\t}\\n185: \\t\\ttotalScaledDown += scaledDownCount\\n186: \\t\\toldRSs[i] = updatedOldRS\\n187: \\t}\\n188: \\treturn oldRSs, totalScaledDown, nil\\n189: }\\n190: \\n191: // scaleDownOldReplicaSetsForRollingUpdate scales down old replica sets when deployment strategy is \\\"RollingUpdate\\\".\\n192: // Need check maxUnavailable to ensure availability\\n193: func (dc *DeploymentController) scaleDownOldReplicaSetsForRollingUpdate(ctx context.Context, allRSs []*apps.ReplicaSet, oldRSs []*apps.ReplicaSet, deployment *apps.Deployment) (int32, error) {\\n194: \\tlogger := klog.FromContext(ctx)\\n195: \\tmaxUnavailable := deploymentutil.MaxUnavailable(*deployment)\\n196: \\n197: \\t// Check if we can scale down.\\n198: \\tminAvailable := *(deployment.Spec.Replicas) -
